## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics where rate laws specify dA_dt as a function of A (reaction order, equilibrium approach) and sometimes explicit time-dependence (time-varying rate constants, forcing). With only t and A available, the most likely structures are single-species decay/production, autocatalysis, and time-dependent effective rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (surface-limited or saturation giving constant depletion rate)
- Zero-order production: dA_dt = c0 (constant feed/source term into A)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- First-order with source: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous production with first-order loss; relaxes to steady state)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or overall second-order in A)
- General power-law (nth-order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall order or chain-branching approximations)
- Mixed-order loss: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order pathways)
- Reversible/relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-form kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating then self-limiting behavior; e.g., autocatalysis or carrying-capacity-like constraint)
- Time-varying first-order rate (exponential ramp): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant changes over time due to external conditions)
- Time-varying first-order rate (decaying activity): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation or diminishing irradiation)
- Periodically forced first-order rate: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (diurnal/periodic forcing of an effective rate constant)
- Induction/activation factor on decay: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate turns on after an induction period)
- Self-inhibition / crowding factor: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (rate increases with A at low A but is inhibited at high A without invoking multi-substrate variables)
- Nonlinear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) * Abs(A - c1)**c2 (sharper-than-linear approach to equilibrium; effective order around equilibrium)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Exponential-in-time concentration trajectories A(t) typically imply dA_dt proportional to A (first-order decay: dA_dt = -c*A).
- A linear A(t) trend over a time window suggests zero-order behavior (dA_dt approximately constant).
- A steady-state/plateau at nonzero A indicates a source–sink balance, often captured by dA_dt = c0 - c1*A or relaxation dA_dt = -c*(A-c_eq).
- If the decay accelerates strongly with higher A (much faster initially than later beyond first-order), include higher powers A**n or mixed orders (-c1*A - c2*A**2).
- Sigmoidal rise/decay (slow start, then fast change, then slowing) is consistent with autocatalytic or self-limiting forms like dA_dt = c*A*(cAmax - A) or induction factors (1 - exp(-c*t)).
- Observable changes in apparent rate over time at fixed A (e.g., early vs late kinetics not explained by A alone) motivate explicit t-dependence multiplying A, such as exp(c*t), exp(-c*t), or sinusoidal modulation.
- If high concentrations inhibit the net rate (initial rate lower than expected from a power law), rational inhibition-like structures such as A/(1 + c*A) can capture crowding or self-inhibition with a single species.
- Approach to equilibrium often appears as dA_dt changing sign around a particular A value; include (A - c_eq) factors to enforce zero net rate at equilibrium.
- If the reaction rate must remain nonpositive (pure consumption), enforce a leading negative sign and avoid additive positive terms unless a physical source term is intended.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK11)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))
Candidate formulas: 61

GT is the fixed function of \(A\):
\[
f(A)= -0.8817392153705143\,A^2 + 0.5984688560365095\,\sin(\sqrt{A})
\]
Key structural facts:
- It contains exactly an \(A^2\) polynomial term and a \(\sin(\sqrt{A})\) term.
- No dependence on \(t\).
- The sine’s argument is \(\sqrt{A}\), not linear in \(A\), not affine in \(A\), not \(\log\), not \(\exp\), not rational.

So any candidate can only match if it can produce \(-kA^2 + b\sin(\sqrt{A})\) **exactly** (for all \(A\)) by choosing its constants, and all other terms must be eliminable (set to 0) without breaking the needed structure.

---

### 1. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2 + c3(A+c4)^{c5}\)
Only powers/polynomials. No sine. Cannot match.

### 2. \(A c0/(A+c1) + A^{c2}c3 + A^{c4}c5\)
Rational + power terms only. No sine. Cannot match.

GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.8817*A² + 0.5985*sin(√A)**

The GT has two terms: a polynomial term (-c₀·A²) and a trigonometric term (c₂·_m·sin(√A)). The key basis functions are **A²** and **sin(√A)**.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. The critical question for each is: can it produce exactly the basis functions A² and sin(√A)?

**Key observations:**
- sin(√A) is NOT the same as sin(A·c), sin(A+c), log(A+1), exp(A·c), √A, A^c, or any rational function of A
- sin(√A) cannot be represented by any combination of polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, or rational functions
- sin(A·c + c) ≠ sin(√A) for all A (different argument structure)

Let me check candidates that contain sin() with potentially matching arguments:

**Candidates with sin():** 11, 15, 22, 23, 31, 33, 34, 37, 44, 46, 49, 51, 54, 59

All of these have sin(A*c + c) as the argument pattern, which is sin(linear function of A). This is NOT equivalent to sin(√A) because √A is not a linear function of A. These cannot match.

**Candidates with A^c terms (power law):** 1, 2, 3, 20, 27, 29, 35, 54, 58, 60

For these, could A^c·c equal sin(√A)? No - A^c is a power function, not a trigonometric function. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

**Candidates with exp():** 7, 14, 16, 21, 24, 28, 30, 32, 39, 41, 43, 45, 48, 52, 53, 60, 61

exp(A·c) cannot equal sin(√A).

**Candidates with log():** 4, 13, 18, 25, 26, 34, 36, 42, 45, 46, 47, 59

log(A·c + 1) cannot equal sin(√A).

**Candidates that are purely rational functions of A:** 3, 5, 6, 8, 9, 10, 12, 17, 25, 26, 36, 38, 40, 47, 50, 55, 56, 57

Rational functions cannot produce sin(√A).

**Candidates with √A + polynomial:** 9, 10, 17, 19, 35

√A is not sin(√A). These cannot match.

**Candidates with t dependence:** 16, 17, 38, 43, 47, 49, 50, 52, 55, 56

GT has no t dependence. Setting t-coefficients to 0 reduces these to other forms already analyzed.

After exhaustive analysis, **none** of the candidates contain sin(√A) or any function that could be algebraically equivalent to sin(√A). The GT requires the specific basis function sin(√A), which is absent from all candidates.
